Its explanations, now part of Phishnet and API CASB, can improve user decisions and SOC efficiency.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;Todayâs security ecosystem generates a staggering amount of complex telemetry. For instance, processing a single email requires analyzing sender reputation, authentication results, link behavior, infrastructure metadata, and countless other attributes. Simultaneously, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/products/casb/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloud access security broker (CASB)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; engines continuously scan SaaS environments for signals that detect misconfigurations, risky access, and exposed data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But while detections have become more sophisticated, explanations have not always kept pace.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Security and IT teams are often aware when something is flagged, but they do not always know, at a glance, why. End users are asked to make real-time decisions about emails that may impact the entire organization, yet they are rarely given clear, contextual guidance in the moment that matters.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/fundamentals/reference/cloudy-ai-agent/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; changes that.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudy is our LLM-powered explanation layer, built directly into Cloudflare One. It translates complex machine learning outputs into precise, human-readable guidance for security teams and end users alike. Instead of exposing raw technical signals, Cloudy surfaces the reasoning behind a detection in a way that drives informed action.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/en-au/sase/products/email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, this means helping users understand why a message was flagged before they escalate it to the security operations center, or SOC. For Cloudflare CASB, it means helping administrators quickly understand the risk and remediation path for SaaS findings without having to manually assess low-level signals.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This post outlines how we are extending Cloudy across &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/email-security/settings/phish-submissions/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Phishnet&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and API CASB to improve decision making, reduce unnecessary noise, and turn complex security signals into clear, actionable insight.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;cloudy-for-email-security-users\&quot;&gt;Cloudy for Email Security users&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#cloudy-for-email-security-users\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;When an email is analyzed by &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/products/email-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Email Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, it is not evaluated by a single signal or model. Instead, a wide range of machine learning models analyze different parts of the message, from sender reputation and message structure to content, links, and behavioral patterns. This model set continues to grow as our machine learning team regularly trains and deploys new detections to keep pace with evolving threats.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Based on this analysis, messages are labeled with outcomes such as Malicious, Suspicious, Spam, Bulk, or Spoof. While these detections have been effective, we consistently heard feedback from customers that it was not always clear why a message was flagged. The decision was correct, they told us âÂ  but the reasoning behind it was often opaque to both end users and security teams.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To address this, we introduced the first version of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudy-driven-email-security-summaries/\&quot;&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;u&gt;: LLM-powered summaries for detections&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. These summaries translate what our machine learning models are seeing into human readable explanations. Initially, these summaries were available in the Cloudflare dashboard to help SOC teams during investigations. Over the past few months, customer feedback has confirmed that these explanations significantly improve understanding in our detections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;As we continued speaking with customers, another challenge surfaced. Our &lt;b&gt;Phishnet&lt;/b&gt; tool allows users to submit messages to the SOC when they believe an email may be suspicious. While this empowers employees to participate in security, many SOC teams told us their queues were being flooded with submissions that turned out to be clean messages.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The result was unnecessary backlog and slower response times for emails that actually required investigation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;At the same time, customers told us that traditional security awareness training was not always enough. Users still struggled to evaluate emails in the moment, when it mattered most. They wanted more contextual guidance directly within the workflow where decisions are made.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This upgrade is designed to address both of these problems. By bringing clearer explanations and contextual education directly into Phishnet, we aim to help users make better decisions while reducing noise for SOC teams, without sacrificing security.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;the-problem-some-users-flag-too-many-emails-while-some-arent-cautious-enough\&quot;&gt;The problem: Some users flag too many emails, while some arenât cautious enough&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-problem-some-users-flag-too-many-emails-while-some-arent-cautious-enough\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;As organizations and attack techniques have evolved, so has the role of the end user. Modern email threats increasingly rely on social engineering, subtle impersonation, and psychological pressure which places users directly in the decision path.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In response, users are being asked to act as an additional layer of defense. However, traditional security awareness tools often fall short. Training is typically delivered through periodic sessions or simulated phishing campaigns, disconnected from real messages and real decisions. When users encounter an unfamiliar email, they are left without enough context to confidently assess risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This gap commonly leads to one of two outcomes. Some users submit nearly every questionable message to the SOC, creating excessive noise and slowing down investigations. Others interact with messages they should not, simply because nothing in the moment signals clear risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;By embedding Cloudy directly into Phishnet, we close this gap.Â &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Users receive immediate, contextual explanations that help them understand what Cloudflare is seeing and why a message may be risky. This enables users to make informed decisions at the point of interaction, reduces unnecessary escalations to the SOC, and allows security teams to focus on the messages that truly require attention.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over time, this approach shifts users from being a source of noise to becoming an effective part of the detection and response workflow. The result: stronger email security, without adding friction or burden to security teams.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;phishnet-for-microsoft-gets-a-cloudy-upgrade\&quot;&gt;Phishnet for Microsoft gets a Cloudy upgrade&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#phishnet-for-microsoft-gets-a-cloudy-upgrade\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;In the next month, we will be upgrading our Phishnet reporting button to extend the Cloudy summaries.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6dO9TV4MfE2R0YZ035QQ7/3693156d65a4c8aca4b2b9d57e77ce87/image1.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;882\&quot; height=\&quot;1768\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;The new Phishnet screens will show Cloudy summaries.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With this upgrade, end users receive a simplified, user-friendly version of Cloudy summaries at the moment they report a message. These summaries are generated in real time using Cloudflare Workers AI and run directly on Cloudflareâs global Workers platform when a user interacts with a message in Phishnet.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When a user clicks the Phishnet reporting button, the request triggers a Workers-based workflow that aggregates structured outputs from multiple detection models associated with that message. These model outputs include signals such as sender reputation, domain and infrastructure characteristics, authentication results, link and content analysis, and behavioral indicators collected during message processing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The aggregated signals are then passed to Workers AI, where a series of purpose-built prompts generate a natural language explanation. Each prompt is designed to transform low-level detection outputs into a concise and human-readable summary. This process focuses on explanation rather than classification and does not alter the original disposition of the message.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5PSAZclxFkdcvSivalmoCn/b355e9e6cf667e6e8e9587f6946db5c6/image6.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;684\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;How Cloudy transforms detections into clear explanations.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For this experience, we intentionally redesigned the summaries compared to those shown to administrators in the Cloudflare dashboard. During testing, we found that admin-focused summaries often relied on technical concepts that were difficult for non-technical users to interpret. Terms such as ASNs, IP reputation, or authentication failures required translation.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To ensure end users can understand the summaries, Phishnet emphasizes plain-language explanations while preserving the meaning of the underlying detections.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Signal&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;What it means&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloudy translation for end users&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;SPF Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Sender explicitly not authorized by SPF&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;This email failed a sender verification check.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DKIM Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Message signature does not validate&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The message integrity check failed, which can be a sign of tampering.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DMARC Fail&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;DMARC policy check failed&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The senderâs domain could not confirm this email is legitimate.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Reply to Mismatch&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Reply To differs from From&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Replies may go to a different address than the sender shown.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain Age&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain recently registered&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The sender domain is newly created, which is common in phishing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;URL Low Reputation&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Destination URL has poor reputation&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;The link destination has signals associated with risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because this workflow runs on the Cloudflare Workers platform, summaries are generated with low latency and at global scale â so users receive immediate feedback at the moment of interaction. This real-time context allows users to better understand why an email may be risky or why it appears safe before deciding whether to escalate it to the SOC.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We are currently beta testing this experience with Microsoft customers to ensure the summaries are accurate and reliable. &lt;b&gt;Cloudy summaries are not trained on customer data.&lt;/b&gt; We are also applying additional validation to ensure the generated explanations do not hallucinate. Accuracy is critical at this stage as incorrect guidance could introduce real security risk.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Following the beta period, we plan to expand access to all Microsoft users. We will also bring similar upgrades to the Phishnet sidebar for Google Workspace users later in 2026.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;your-casb-findings-explained-with-cloudy\&quot;&gt;Your CASB findings, explained with Cloudy&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#your-casb-findings-explained-with-cloudy\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;But helping end users better understand what makes an email risky is only part of the story. We are also applying Cloudy to the administrative side of security operations, where clarity and speed matter just as much. Beyond Phishnet, Cloudy now translates complex CASB findings into structured explanations that help security and IT teams quickly understand risk, prioritize remediation, and take confident action across their SaaS environments.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;api-casb-in-the-wild\&quot;&gt;API CASB in the wild&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#api-casb-in-the-wild\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Inside &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/sase/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, our SASE platform, CASB connects to the SaaS and cloud tools your teams already use. By talking to providers over API, CASB gives security and IT teams:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;A consolidated view of misconfigurations, overshared files, and risky access patterns across apps like Microsoft 365, Google Workspace, Slack, Salesforce, Box, GitHub, Jira, and Confluence (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/applications/scan-apps/casb-integrations/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CASB Integrations&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Continuous scanning for new issues as users collaborate, share, and adopt new tools.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Findings that are organized, searchable, and exportable for triage and reporting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1CH5fnjMQL3oK5PdF9F1bT/d34abcaa64d536cd8706a407f20ba2a9/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1429\&quot; height=\&quot;806\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sub&gt;&lt;i&gt;A typical CASB Findings page showing detections for a Microsoft 365 finding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;making-saas-security-straightforward\&quot;&gt;Making SaaS security straightforward&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#making-saas-security-straightforward\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Until now, understanding what exactly triggered a CASB Finding â the detections that CASB makes across connected SaaS integrations â has been a black box. While the information was there to put together an explanation of why that file, that user, that configuration was triggering a CASB Finding Type, it wasnât exactly obvious the reason why it was ultimately detected by our system.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With the introduction of Cloudy summaries in CASB, users receive a short description of the detection rationale with the specific details of the match listed out for easy comprehension.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Unlike a simple text summary, Cloudy for CASB provides a structured breakdown designed for immediate remediation. As seen in our beta testing across different providers, from Microsoft 365 to Dropbox, the model consistently parses findings into two distinct sections:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: It identifies exactly why the finding matters. For instance, rather than just noting a &amp;#39;Suspended User,&amp;#39; Cloudy clarifies that this &amp;#39;may indicate a compromised account or a user who should no longer have access to company data&amp;#39;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: It offers immediate next steps. Instead of generic advice, it suggests specific actions, such as verifying if a suspension was intentional or reviewing an application&amp;#39;s legitimacy before revoking access.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This structure ensures that analysts can understand the gravity of a finding without needing deep expertise in the specific SaaS application involved.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/BkfPI5VWYYaGzjjHsfyEz/16783ef841292ff66972222afda350e9/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; Finding.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Finding Type&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Technical Signal&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloudy Translation (Risk &amp;amp; Guidance)&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Identity &amp;amp; Access&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Dropbox:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Suspended User&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: A suspended user account may indicate a access has been properly revoked.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Shadow IT&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Google data.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Review the application&amp;#39;s legitimacy and necessity, and consider revoking access if it is no longer needed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Email Security&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Microsoft 365:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Domain DMARC record not present&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: The absence of a DMARC record may leave the domain vulnerable to email spoofing and phishing attacks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Configure a DMARC record for the domain to specify how to handle unauthenticated emails.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Data Loss Prevention&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Microsoft 365:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;File publicly accessible + DLP Match&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;Risk: This file being shared publicly with edit access may allow unauthorized modifications... especially given the potential sensitive content indicated by the DLP Profile match.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Guidance: Review the file&amp;#39;s content... and consider restricting access if necessary.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;We know that when it comes to our customers getting to the bottom of identified security issues, time is of the essence. We believe that any amount of unnecessary uncertainty or lack of clarity around whatâs going wrong just puts more time between an imperfect state and one that is more secure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We built this feature on the same privacy-first foundations as all products at Cloudflare. Cloudy summaries in CASB are generated using Cloudflare Workers AI, ensuring that your data remains within our secure infrastructure during analysis. The models are not trained on your SaaS data, and the summaries are generated ephemerally to aid in triage. This allows your team to leverage the speed of AI without exposing sensitive internal documents or configurations to public models.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;whats-next\&quot;&gt;Whatâs next&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;For Email Security, we will continue to expand how Cloudy supports both administrators and end users. Our focus is on delivering clearer explanations, better in context guidance, and deeper integration into daily workflows.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For CASB, weâre excited to look for opportunities where Cloudy can make it even easier for CASB administrators to understand whatâs going on across their cloud and SaaS apps. Keep an eye out as we look to expand Cloudy coverage to allow administrators to query their findings using natural language, further reducing the time it takes to identify and remediate risks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Looking ahead, this includes richer explanations for additional detection types, tighter feedback loops between user actions and detections, and continued improvements to how users and SOC teams collaborate through Phishnet. Our goal is to make Cloudy a core part of how organizations understand, trust, and act on email security decisions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We provide all organizations (whether a Cloudflare customer or not) with free access to our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/email-security/retro-scan/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Retro Scan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; tool, allowing them to use our predictive AI models to scan existing inbox messages in Microsoft 365.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Retro Scan will detect and highlight any threats found, enabling organizations to remediate them directly in their email accounts. Security&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or their preferred solution, to prevent similar threats from reaching their inboxes in the future.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;If you are interested in how Cloudflare can help Page for Locale&quot;]}],&quot;url&quot;:[0,&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudy-upgrades-for-cloudflare-one&quot;],&quot;metadata&quot;:[0,{&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;How Cloudy translates complex security into human action&quot;],&quot;description&quot;:[0,&quot;Cloudy is our LLM-powered explanation layer built directly into Cloudflare One. Its explanations, now part of Phishnet and API CASB, can improve user decisions and SOC efficiency.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/4plooiLyILg6Jg48r5v3ke/87710382aecbbe84725ee9ad853caf5e/OG_Share_2024-2025-2026__8_.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;5NwDf8fspgoSx9Pgcx1xLy&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;ASPA: making Internet routing more secure&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;aspa-secure-internet&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;ASPA is the cryptographic upgrade for BGP that helps prevent route leaks by verifying the path network traffic takes. New features in Cloudflare Radar make tracking its adoption easy.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;Internet traffic relies on the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/glossary/what-is-bgp/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Border Gateway Protocol (BGP)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to find its way between networks. However, this traffic can sometimes be misdirected due to configuration errors or malicious actions. When traffic is routed through networks it was not intended to pass through, it is known as a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7908\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;route leak&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. We have &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/bgp-route-leak-venezuela/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;written on our blog&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-1111-incident-on-june-27-2024/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;multiple times&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; about &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/route-leak-detection-with-cloudflare-radar/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;BGP route leaks&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and the impact they have on Internet routing, and a few times we have even alluded to a future of path verification in BGP.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;While the network community has made significant progress in verifying the final destination of Internet traffic, securing the actual path it takes to get there remains a key challenge for maintaining a reliable Internet. To address this, the industry is adopting a new cryptographic standard called &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-sidrops-aspa-verification/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ASPA (Autonomous System Provider Authorization)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which is designed to validate the entire path of network traffic and prevent route leaks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To help the community track the rollout of this standard, Cloudflare Radar has introduced a new ASPA deployment monitoring feature. This view allows users to observe ASPA adoption trends over time across the five&lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_Internet_registry\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt; Regional Internet Registries (RIRs)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and view ASPA records and changes over time at the&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/what-is-an-autonomous-system/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt; Autonomous System (AS)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; level.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-is-aspa\&quot;&gt;What is ASPA?&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-is-aspa\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;To understand how ASPA works, it is helpful to look at how the Internet currently secures traffic destinations.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, networks use a secure infrastructure system called &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Public_Key_Infrastructure\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RPKI (Resource Public Key Infrastructure)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, which has seen &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.apnic.net/2026/02/20/rpkis-2025-year-in-review/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;significant deployment growth&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; over the past few years. Within RPKI, networks publish specific cryptographic records called ROAs (Route Origin Authorizations). A ROA acts as a verifiable digital ID card, confirming that an Autonomous System (AS) is officially authorized to announce specific IP addresses. This addresses the &amp;quot;origin hijacks&amp;quot; issue, where one network attempts to impersonate another.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-sidrops-aspa-verification/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ASPA (Autonomous System Provider Authorization)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; builds directly on this foundation. While a ROA verifies the &lt;i&gt;destination&lt;/i&gt;, an ASPA record verifies the &lt;i&gt;journey&lt;/i&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When data travels across the Internet, it keeps a running log of every network it passes through. In BGP, this log is known as the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc4271#section-5.1.2\&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS_PATH&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (Autonomous System Path). ASPA provides networks with a way to officially publish a list of their authorized upstream providers within the RPKI system. This allows any receiving network to look at the &lt;code&gt;AS_PATH&lt;/code&gt;, check the associated ASPA records, and verify that the traffic only traveled through an approved chain of networks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;A ROA helps ensure the traffic arrives at the correct destination, ASPA ensures the traffic takes an intended, authorized route to get there. Letâs take a look at how path evaluation actually works in practice.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;route-leak-detection-with-aspa\&quot;&gt;Route leak detection with ASPA&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#route-leak-detection-with-aspa\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;How does ASPA know if a route is a &lt;i&gt;detour&lt;/i&gt;? It relies on the hierarchy of the Internet.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In a healthy Internet routing topology (e.g. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://ieeexplore.ieee.org/document/6363987\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;âvalley-freeâ routing&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;), traffic generally follows a specific path: it travels &amp;quot;up&amp;quot; from a customer to a large provider (like a major ISP), optionally crosses over to another big provider, and then flows &amp;quot;down&amp;quot; to the destination. You can visualize this as a âmountainâ shape:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The Up-Ramp:&lt;/b&gt; Traffic starts at a Customer and travels &amp;quot;up&amp;quot; through larger and larger Providers (ISPs), where ISPs pay other ISPs to transit traffic for them.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The Apex:&lt;/b&gt; It reaches the top tier of the Internet backbone and may cross a single peering link.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The Down-Ramp:&lt;/b&gt; It travels &amp;quot;down&amp;quot; through providers to reach the destination Customer.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1VGuSHfq6GcQZUYLGmoDH3/a1486f40c16e568f32ca2fa81d58ac41/1.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1540\&quot; height=\&quot;636\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;A visualization of &amp;quot;valley-free&amp;quot; routing. Routes propagate up to a provider, optionally across one peering link, and down to a customer.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In this model, a route leak is like a valley, or dip. One type of such leak happens when traffic goes down to a customer and then unexpectedly tries to go back &lt;i&gt;up&lt;/i&gt; to another provider. &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6eoaEpdIJpCCLbMnNZD5ob/7ceca2a98f2252e8161915b942bf7dbd/2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1548\&quot; height=\&quot;706\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;This &amp;quot;down-and-up&amp;quot; movement is undesirable as customers aren&amp;#39;t intended nor equipped to transit traffic between two larger network providers.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;how-aspa-validation-works\&quot;&gt;How ASPA validation works&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-aspa-validation-works\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;ASPA gives network operators a cryptographic way to declare their &lt;i&gt;authorized providers,&lt;/i&gt; enabling receiving networks to verify that an AS path follows this expected structure.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;ASPA validates AS paths by checking the âchain of relationshipsâ from both ends of the routes propagation:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Checking the Up-Ramp:&lt;/b&gt; The check starts at the origin and moves forward. At every hop, it asks: &lt;i&gt;&amp;quot;Did this network authorize the next network as a Provider?&amp;quot;&lt;/i&gt; It keeps going until the chain stops.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Checking the Down-Ramp:&lt;/b&gt; It does the same thing from the destination of a BGP update, moving backward.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;If the &amp;quot;Up&amp;quot; path and the &amp;quot;Down&amp;quot; path overlap or meet at the top, the route is &lt;b&gt;Valid&lt;/b&gt;. The mountain shape is intact.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;However, if the two valid paths &lt;b&gt;do not meet&lt;/b&gt;, i.e. there is a gap in the middle where authorization is missing or invalid, ASPA reports such paths as problematic. That gap represents the &amp;quot;valley&amp;quot; or the leak.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h4 id=\&quot;validation-process-example\&quot;&gt;Validation process example&lt;/h4&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#validation-process-example\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Letâs look at a scenario where a network (AS65539) receives a bad route from a customer (AS65538).&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7kn8W6c7CaPcMLMycjS5NO/59036dc52a942870e9bb0e377f235dd4/3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1122\&quot; height=\&quot;890\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;The customer (AS65538) is trying to send traffic received from one provider (AS65537) &amp;quot;up&amp;quot; to another provider (AS65538), acting like a bridge between providers. This is a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc7908#autoid-4\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;classic route leak&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Now letâs walk the ASPA validation process.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We check the &lt;b&gt;Up-Ramp&lt;/b&gt;: The original source (AS65536) authorizes its provider. (Check passes).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We check the &lt;b&gt;Down-Ramp&lt;/b&gt;: We start from the destination and look back. We see the customer (AS65538).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The Mismatch:&lt;/b&gt; The up-ramp ends at AS65537, while the down-ramp ends at 65538. The two ramps do not connect.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because the &amp;quot;Up&amp;quot; path and &amp;quot;Down&amp;quot; path fail to connect, the system flags this as ASPA &lt;b&gt;Invalid&lt;/b&gt;. ASPA is required to do this path validation, as without signed ASPA objects in RPKI, we cannot find which networks are authorized to advertise which prefixes to whom. By signing a list of provider networks for each AS, we know which networks should be able to propagate prefixes laterally or upstream.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;aspa-against-forged-origin-hijacks\&quot;&gt;ASPA against forged-origin hijacks&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#aspa-against-forged-origin-hijacks\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;ASPA can serve as an effective defense against &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.usenix.org/conference/nsdi24/presentation/holterbach\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;forged-origin hijacks&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, where an attacker bypasses Route Origin Validation (ROV) by pretending and advertising a BGP path to a real origin prefix. Although the origin AS remains correct, the relationship between the hijacker and the victim is fabricated.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6MNVRoNDzxlHDVGTP2nRPw/87485ad246baa734eef3192fd48012a8/4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1402\&quot; height=\&quot;862\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;ASPA exposes this deception by allowing the victim network to cryptographically declare its actual authorized providers; because the hijacker is not on that authorized list, the path is rejected as invalid, effectively preventing the malicious redirection.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2KGtsKWBdlNFySIswRb5rD/d26b266c2dc942be9b9f6c6ec383843b/5.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1159\&quot; height=\&quot;862\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;ASPA cannot fully protect against forged-origin hijacks, however. There is still at least one case where not even ASPA validation can fully prevent this type of attack on a network. An example of a forged-origin hijack that ASPA cannot account for is when a provider forges a path advertisement &lt;i&gt;to their customer.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3DPYEXwSUPmWUWvsyxFJHX/b059dae85cf764fdcd5a5257f5ebc373/6.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1795\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Essentially, a provider could âfakeâ a peering link with another AS to attract traffic from a customer with a short AS_PATH length, even when no such peering link exists. ASPA does not prevent this path forgery by the provider, because ASPA only works off of provider information and knows nothing specific about peering relationships.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;So while ASPA can be an effective means of rejecting forged-origin hijack routes, there are still some rare cases where it will be ineffective, and those are worth noting.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;creating-aspa-objects-just-a-few-clicks-away\&quot;&gt;Creating ASPA objects: just a few clicks away&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#creating-aspa-objects-just-a-few-clicks-away\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Creating an ASPA object for your network (or Autonomous System) is now a simple process in registries like &lt;a href=\&quot;https://labs.ripe.net/author/tim_bruijnzeels/aspa-in-the-rpki-dashboard-a-new-layer-of-routing-security/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RIPE&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.arin.net/announcements/20260120/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ARIN&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. All you need is your AS number and the AS numbers of the providers you purchase Internet transit service from. These are the authorized upstream networks you trust to announce your IP addresses to the wider Internet. In the opposite direction, these are also the networks you authorize to send you a full routing table, which acts as the complete map of how to reach the rest of the Internet.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Weâd like to show you just how easy creating an ASPA object is with a quick example.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Say we need to create the ASPA object for AS203898, an AS we use for our Cloudflare London office Internet. At the time of writing we have three Internet providers for the office: AS8220, AS2860, and AS1273. This means we will create an ASPA object for AS203898 with those three provider members in a list.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;First, we log into the RIPE &lt;a href=\&quot;https://dashboard.rpki.ripe.net/#overview\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RPKI dashboard&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and navigate to the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://dashboard.rpki.ripe.net/#aspa\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ASPA&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; section:&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3CCFItZpP8JbYCotDGfuM3/c7ad0041ceea4f48c37ff59f416f8242/7.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;946\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Then, we click on âCreate ASPAâ for the object we want to create an ASPA object for. From there, we just fill in the providers for that AS. &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6ABmfhRQQRbLhMat6Ug01K/3a9d73ad8ade315416c4cc6eb9073ada/8.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;946\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Itâs as simple as that. After just a short period of waiting, we can query the global RPKI ecosystem and find our ASPA object for AS203898 with the providers we defined.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/xAKD1b704fg7SMxeg867P/59ce564867565331e2d531de15dc7e87/Screenshot_2026-02-27_at_11.09.55.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1666\&quot; height=\&quot;304\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Itâs a similar story with &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.arin.net/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ARIN&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, the only other &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_Internet_registry\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Regional Internet Registries (RIRs)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that currently supports the creation of ASPA objects. Log in to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://account.arin.net/public/login\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;ARIN online,&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; then navigate to Routing Security, and click âManage RPKIâ.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/PTCdyldcTc1Uc0iazZlg4/51ed97a8ef0d095b947f7ab2bf4b1fd3/9.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1966\&quot; height=\&quot;748\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;From there, youâll be able to click on âCreate ASPAâ. In this example, we will create an object for another one of our ASNs, AS400095.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/4bLLHAeU4Eaz6RPgSPDzn9/a482b6c7ed4ef78f7346ca80c9a5ba46/10.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1928\&quot; height=\&quot;900\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;And thatâs it â now we have created our ASPA object for AS40095 with provider AS0.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/9yOZPpMH4olQXu2DNpJPO/cca432fd82e61c6492987b7ccedbdc57/11.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1966\&quot; height=\&quot;972\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6emDXxMbU0BSKk5BVXUdJ6/132b9a7279b93e3ae0329dec83a9bfac/Screenshot_2026-02-27_at_11.11.31.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1676\&quot; height=\&quot;296\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;The âAS0â provider entry is special when used, and means the AS owner attests there are &lt;b&gt;no&lt;/b&gt; valid upstream providers for their network. By definition this means every transit-free Tier-1 network should eventually sign an ASPA with only âAS0â in their object, if they truly only have peer and customer relationships.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;new-aspa-features-in-cloudflare-radar\&quot;&gt;New ASPA features in Cloudflare RadarÂ &lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#new-aspa-features-in-cloudflare-radar\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;We have added a new ASPA deployment monitoring feature to &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Radar&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. The new ASPA deployment view allows users to examine the growth of ASPA adoption over time, with the ability to visualize trends across the five &lt;a href=\&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_Internet_registry\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Regional Internet Registries&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (RIRs) based on AS registration. &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7FoW86CVloqBqZO7wcOiq8/f5f2973db227b8184127f76fdad64dc4/12.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1600\&quot; height=\&quot;876\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;We have also integrated ASPA data directly into the country/region and ASN routing pages. Users can now track how different locations are progressing in securing their infrastructure, based on the associated ASPA records from the customer ASNs registered locally.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1tBhOpIxc6tNOJXWPPAk4U/7c334c9ddb089eb823ce23eb49ddbdc3/13.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1848\&quot; height=\&quot;1456\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;There are also new features when you zoom into a particular Autonomous System (AS), for example &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/routing/AS203898#connectivity\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;AS203898&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/7nTBPD0PgzPOS0eOxpG3rW/65d9b312be2e81e4c59164c98b7b6276/14.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;837\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;We can see whether a networkâs observed BGP upstream providers are ASPA authorized, their full list of providers in their ASPA object, and the timeline of ASPA changes that involve their AS.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;the-road-to-better-routing-security\&quot;&gt;The road to better routing security&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-road-to-better-routing-security\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;With ASPA finally becoming a reality, we have our cryptographic upgrade for Internet path validation. However, those who have been around since the start of RPKI for route origin validation know &lt;a href=\&quot;https://manrs.org/2023/05/estimating-the-timeline-for-aspa-deployment/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;this will be a long road&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to actually providing significant value on the Internet. Changes are needed to RPKI Relaying Party (RP) packages, signer implementations, RTR (RPKI-to-Router protocol) software, and BGP implementations to actually use ASPA objects and validate paths with them.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In addition to ASPA adoption, operators should also configure BGP roles as described within &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/rfc9234/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC9234&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. The BGP roles configured on BGP sessions will help future ASPA implementations on routers &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/draft-ietf-sidrops-aspa-verification-24#section-6.3\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;decide which algorithm to apply&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;: &lt;i&gt;upstream&lt;/i&gt; or &lt;i&gt;downstream&lt;/i&gt;. In other words, BGP roles give us the power as operators to directly tie our intended BGP relationships with another AS to sessions with those neighbors. Check with your routing vendors and make sure they support &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/rfc9234/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC9234 BGP roles and OTC&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (Only-to-Customer) attribute implementation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To get the most out of ASPA, we encourage everyone to create their ASPA objects for their AS&lt;i&gt;. &lt;/i&gt;Creating and maintaining these ASPA objects requires careful attention. In the future, as networks use these records to actively block invalid paths, omitting a legitimate provider could cause traffic to be dropped. However, managing this risk is no different from how networks already handle Route Origin Authorizations (ROAs) today. ASPA is the necessary cryptographic upgrade for Internet path validation, and weâre happy itâs
