This extends post-quantum encryption across all major Cloudflare One on-ramps and off-ramps.&quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;During Security Week 2025, we launched the industryâs first cloud-native&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/press/press-releases/2025/cloudflare-advances-industrys-first-cloud-native-quantum-safe-zero-trust/\&quot;&gt; &lt;u&gt;post-quantum Secure Web Gateway (SWG) and Zero Trust solution&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, a major step towards securing enterprise network traffic sent from end user devices to public and private networks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;But this is only part of the equation. To truly secure the future of enterprise networking, you need a complete &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/access-management/what-is-sase/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Secure Access Service Edge (SASE)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, we complete the equation: Cloudflare One is the first SASE platform to support modern standards-compliant post-quantum (PQ) encryption in our Secure Web Gateway, and across Zero Trust and Wide Area Network (WAN) use cases.Â  More specifically, Cloudflare One now offers post-quantum hybrid ML-KEM (Module-Lattice-based Key-Encapsulation Mechanism) across all major on-ramps and off-ramps.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To complete the equation, we added support for post-quantum encryption to our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/reference/gre-ipsec-tunnels/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare IPsec&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (our cloud-native WAN-as-a-Service) and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/configuration/connector/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One Appliance&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (our physical or virtual WAN appliance that establish Cloudflare IPsec connections). Cloudflare IPsec uses the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/what-is-ipsec/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;IPsec&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; protocol to establish encrypted tunnels from a customerâs network to Cloudflareâs global network, while IP &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/cdn/glossary/anycast-network/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Anycast&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is used to automatically route that tunnel to the nearest Cloudflare data center. Cloudflare IPsec simplifies configuration and provides high availability; if a specific data center becomes unavailable, traffic is automatically rerouted to the closest healthy data center. Cloudflare IPsec runs at the scale of our global network, and supports site-to-site across a WAN as well as outbound connections to the Internet.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/configuration/connector/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One Appliance&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; upgrade is generally available as of appliance version 2026.2.0. The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/reference/gre-ipsec-tunnels/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare IPsec&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; upgrade is in closed beta, and you can request access by adding your name to our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/security-week/pq-ipsec-beta/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;closed beta list&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;post-quantum-cryptography-matters-now\&quot;&gt;Post-quantum cryptography matters now&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#post-quantum-cryptography-matters-now\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Quantum threats are not a &amp;quot;next decade&amp;quot; problem. Here is why our customers are prioritizing &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/quantum/what-is-post-quantum-cryptography/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;post-quantum cryptography (PQC)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; today:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;The deadline is approaching. &lt;/b&gt;At the end of 2024, the National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) sent a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/ir/2024/NIST.IR.8547.ipd.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;clear signal&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (that has been &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.bsi.bund.de/EN/Service-Navi/Presse/Pressemitteilungen/Presse2024/241127_Post-Quantum_Cryptography.html\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;echoed&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; by other &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.ncsc.gov.uk/guidance/pqc-migration-timelines\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;agencies&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;): the era of classical public-key cryptography is coming to an end. NIST set a 2030 deadline for depreciating RSA and Elliptic Curve Cryptography (ECC) and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/pqc/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;transitioning to PQC&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that cannot be broken by powerful quantum computers. Organizations that haven&amp;#39;t begun their migration risk being out of compliance and vulnerable as the deadline nears.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Upgrades have historically been tricky. &lt;/b&gt;While 2030 might seem far away, upgrading cryptographic algorithms is notoriously difficult. History has shown us that depreciating cryptography can take decades: we found examples of &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/radius-udp-vulnerable-md5-attack/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;MD5 causing problems 20 years after it was deprecated&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. This lack of crypto agility â the ability to easily swap out cryptographic algorithms â is a major bottleneck. By integrating PQ encryption directly into &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/zero-trust/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, our SASE platform, we provide built-in crypto agility, simplifying how organizations offer remote access and site-to-site connectivity.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Data may already be at risk.&lt;/b&gt; Finally, &amp;quot;Harvest Now, Decrypt Later&amp;quot; is a present and persistent threat, where attackers harvest sensitive network traffic today and then store it until quantum computers become powerful enough to decrypt it. If your data has a shelf life of more than a few years (e.g. financial information, health data, state secrets) it is already at risk unless it is protected by PQ encryption.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;the-two-migrations-on-the-road-to-quantum-safety-key-agreement-and-digital-signatures\&quot;&gt;The two migrations on the road to quantum safety: key agreement and digital signatures&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-two-migrations-on-the-road-to-quantum-safety-key-agreement-and-digital-signatures\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Transitioning network traffic to post-quantum cryptography (PQC) requires an overhaul of two cryptographic primitives: key agreement and digital signatures.Â Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Migration 1: Key establishment. &lt;/b&gt;Key agreement allows two parties to establish a shared secret over an insecure channel; the shared secret is then used to encrypt network traffic, resulting in post-quantum encryption. The industry has largely converged on ML-KEM (Module-Lattice-based Key-Encapsulation Mechanism) as the standard PQ key agreement protocol.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;ML-KEM has been widely adopted for use in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/transport-layer-security-tls/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;TLS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, usually deployed alongside classical Elliptic Curve Diffie Hellman (ECDHE), where the key used to encrypt network traffic is derived by mixing the outputs of the ML-KEM and ECDHE key agreements. (This is also known as âhybrid ML-KEMâ). Well over &lt;a href=\&quot;https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage#post-quantum-encryption\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;60% of human-generated TLS traffic&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to Cloudflareâs network is currently protected with hybrid ML-KEM. The transition to hybrid ML-KEM has been successful because it:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;stops &amp;quot;harvest-now, decrypt-later&amp;quot; attacks&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;does not require specialized hardware or specialized physical connectivity between client and server, unlike approaches like &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/you-dont-need-quantum-hardware/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Quantum Key Distribution (QKD)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;has &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/you-dont-need-quantum-hardware/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;little impact on performance&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, even for short-lived TLS connections&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Because ML-KEM runs in &lt;i&gt;parallel &lt;/i&gt;with classical ECDHE, there is no reduction in security and compliance as compared to the classical ECDHE approach.Â Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Migration 2: Digital signatures. &lt;/b&gt;Meanwhile, digital signatures and certificates protect authenticity, stopping active adversaries from impersonating the server to the client. Unfortunately, PQ signatures are currently larger in size than classical ECC algorithms, which has slowed their adoption. Fortunately, the migration to PQ signatures is less urgent, because PQ signatures are designed to stop active adversaries armed with powerful quantum computers, which are not known to exist yet. Thus, while Cloudflare is actively contributing to the standardization and rollout of PQ digital signatures, the current Cloudflare IPsec upgrade focuses on upgrading key establishment to hybrid ML-KEM.Â Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The U.S. Cybersecurity &amp;amp; Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA) recognized the nature of these two migrations in its &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cisa.gov/resources-tools/resources/product-categories-technologies-use-post-quantum-cryptography-standards\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;January 2026 publication&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, âProduct Categories for Technologies That Use Post-Quantum Cryptography Standards.â&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;breaking-new-ground-with-ipsec\&quot;&gt;Breaking new ground with IPsecÂ &lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#breaking-new-ground-with-ipsec\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;To achieve a SASE fully protected with post-quantum encryption, weâve upgraded our Cloudflare IPsec products to support hybrid ML-KEM in the IPsec protocol.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The IPsec communityâs journey toward post-quantum cryptography has been very different from that of TLS. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/transport-layer-security-tls/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;TLS&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is the de facto standard for encrypting public Internet traffic at Layer 4Â  â e.g. from a browser to a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/cdn/what-is-a-cdn/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;content delivery network (CDN)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; â so security and vendor interoperability are at the forefront of its design. Meanwhile, IPsec is a Layer 3 protocol that commonly connects devices built by the same vendor (e.g. two routers), so interoperability has historically been less of a concern. With this in mind, letâs take a look at IPsecâs journey into the quantum future.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;pre-shared-keys-quantum-key-distribution\&quot;&gt;Pre-Shared Keys? Quantum key distribution?&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#pre-shared-keys-quantum-key-distribution\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc8784\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC 8784&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, published in May 2020, was intended to be the post-quantum update to IPsec Internet Key Exchange v2 (IKEv2), which is used to establish the symmetric keys used to encrypt IPsec network traffic. RFC 8784 implies the use of either long-lived pre-shared keys (PSK) or quantum key distribution (QKD). Neither of these approaches are very palatable.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;RFC 8784 proposes mixing a PSK with a key derived from Diffie Hellman Exchange (DHE), essentially running PSK in hybrid with DHE. This approach protects against harvest-now-decrypt-later attackers, but does not offer &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/staying-on-top-of-tls-attacks/#forward-secrecy\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;forward secrecy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; against quantum adversaries.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/staying-on-top-of-tls-attacks/#forward-secrecy\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Forward secrecy&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; is a standard desideratum of key agreement protocols. It ensures that a system is secure even if the long-lived key is leaked. The PSK approach in RFC 8784 is vulnerable to an harvest-now-decrypt-later adversary that also obtains a copy of a long-lived PSK, and can then decrypt traffic in the future (by breaking the DHE key agreement) once powerful quantum computers become available.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;To solve this forward secrecy issue, RFC 8784 can instead be used to mix the key from the classical DHE with a freshly generated key derived from a QKD protocol.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;QKD uses quantum mechanics to establish a shared, secret cryptographic key between two parties. Importantly, for QKD to work, the parties must have specialized hardware or be connected by a dedicated physical connection. This is a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/you-dont-need-quantum-hardware/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;significant limitation&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, rendering QKD useless for common Internet use cases like connecting a laptop to a distant server over Wi-Fi. These limitations are also why we never invested in deploying QKD for Cloudflare IPsec. The U.S. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.nsa.gov/Cybersecurity/Quantum-Key-Distribution-QKD-and-Quantum-Cryptography-QC/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;National Security Agency (NSA)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.bsi.bund.de/EN/Themen/Unternehmen-und-Organisationen/Informationen-und-Empfehlungen/Quantentechnologien-und-Post-Quanten-Kryptografie/quantentechnologien-und-post-quanten-kryptografie_node.html\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Germanyâs BSI&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.ncsc.gov.uk/whitepaper/quantum-security-technologies\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;UK National Cyber Security Centre&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; have also warned against relying solely on QKD.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;but-what-about-interoperability\&quot;&gt;But what about interoperability?Â &lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#but-what-about-interoperability\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc9370\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;RFC 9370&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; landed in May 2023, specifying the use of hybrid key agreement rather than PSK or QKD. But unlike TLS, which only supports using post-quantum ML-KEM in parallel with classical DHE, this IPsec standard allows using up to &lt;i&gt;seven different key agreements to run at the same time&lt;/i&gt; in parallel with classical Diffie Helman. Moreover, it doesn&amp;#39;t specify details about what these key agreements should be, leaving it up to the vendors to choose their algorithms and implementations. Palo Alto Networks, for example, took this seriously and built support for over &lt;a href=\&quot;https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/compatibility-matrix/reference/supported-cipher-suites/cipher-suites-supported-in-pan-os-11-2/cipher-suites-supported-in-pan-os-11-2-ipsec\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;seven different PQC ciphersuites&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; into its next generation firewall (NGFW), most of which do not interoperate with other vendors and some of which have not yet been standardized by NIST.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Over the years, TLS has gone in the opposite direction, reducing the number of registered ciphersuites from hundreds in TLS 1.2, down to around five in TLS 1.3. This philosophy of reducing âciphersuite bloatâ is also in line with NISTâs &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-52r2.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 800 52&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; from 2019.Â  The rationale for reducing âciphersuite bloatâ includes:Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Improved interoperability across vendors and regions&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Lower risk of attacks that exploit downgrades to weak ciphersuitesÂ &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Lower risk of security problems due to misconfiguration&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Lower risk of implementation flaws by reducing the size of the codebase&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is why we didnât initially build support for RFC 9370.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;standards-that-are-finally-on-the-right-track\&quot;&gt;Standards that are finally on the right track&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#standards-that-are-finally-on-the-right-track\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Itâs also why we were excited when the IPsec community put forth &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. This Internet-Draft standardizes PQ exchange for IPsec in the same way PQ key exchange has been widely deployed for TLS: hybrid ML-KEM. The new draft fills in the gaps in RFC 9370, by specifying how to run the ML-KEM as the additional key exchange in parallel with classical Diffie Hellman in IKEv2.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Now that this specification is available, weâve moved forward with supporting post-quantum IPsec in our Cloudflare IPsec products.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;cloudflare-ipsec-goes-post-quantum\&quot;&gt;Cloudflare IPsec goes post-quantum&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#cloudflare-ipsec-goes-post-quantum\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Cloudflare IPsec is a WAN &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/network-as-a-service-naas/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Network-as-a-Service&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; solution that replaces legacy private network architectures by connecting data centers, branch offices, and cloud VPCs to Cloudflareâs global IP Anycast network.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;With Cloudflare IPsec, Cloudflareâs network acts as the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc5996\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;IKEv2&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; Responder, awaiting connection requests from an IPsec initiator, which is a branch connector device in the customerâs network. Cloudflare IPsec supports IPsec sessions initiated by branch connectors that include our own Cloudflare One Appliance, along with branch connectors from a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/reference/device-compatibility/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;diverse set of vendors&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, including Cisco, Juniper, Palo Alto Networks, Fortinet, Aruba and others.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Weâve implemented production hybrid ML-KEM support in the Cloudflare IPsec IKEv2 Responder, as specified in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. The draft requires a first key exchange to run using a classical Diffie Helman key exchange. The derived key is used to encrypt a second key exchange that is run using ML-KEM. Finally, the keys derived by the two exchanges are mixed and the result is used to secure the data plane traffic in IPsec ESP (Encapsulating Security Payload) mode. ESP mode uses symmetric cryptography and is thus already quantum safe without any additional upgrades.Â  Weâve tested our implementation against the IPsec Initiator in the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://strongswan.org/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;strongswan&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; reference implementation.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can see the ciphersuite used in the IKEv2 negotiation by viewing the Cloudflare &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/logpush/logpush-job/datasets/account/ipsec_logs/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;IPsec logs&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;We chose to implement hybrid ML-KEM rather than âpureâ ML-KEM, i.e. only ML-KEM without DHE running in parallel, for two reasons. First, weâve used hybrid ML-KEM across all of our other Cloudflare products, since this is the approach adopted across the TLS community. And second, it provides a âbelt-and-suspendersâ security: ML-KEM provides protection against quantum harvest-now-decrypt-later attacks, while DHE provides a tried-and-true algorithm against non-quantum adversaries.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;an-invitation-for-interoperability\&quot;&gt;An invitation for interoperability&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#an-invitation-for-interoperability\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The full value of this implementation can be realized only via interoperability. For this reason, we are inviting other vendors that are building out support for IPsec Initiators in their branch connectors per &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to test against our Cloudflare IPsec implementation. Cloudflare customers looking to test out interoperability with third-party branch connectors while we are in closed beta can &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/security-week/pq-ipsec-beta/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;sign up here&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. We plan to GA and build out interoperability with other vendors as more begin to come online with support for &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;quantum-safe-hardware-the-cloudflare-one-appliance\&quot;&gt;Quantum-safe hardware: the Cloudflare One Appliance&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#quantum-safe-hardware-the-cloudflare-one-appliance\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;Many of our customers purchase their branch connector (hardware or virtualized) from Cloudflare, rather than a third-party vendor. Thatâs why the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/magic-wan/configuration/connector/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare One Appliance&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; â our plug-and-play appliance that connects your local network to Cloudflare One â has also been upgraded with post-quantum encryption.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare One Appliance does not use IKEv2 for key agreement or session establishment, opting instead to rely on TLS. The appliance periodically initiates a TLS handshake with the Cloudflare edge, shares a symmetric secret over the resulting TLS connection, then injects that symmetric secret into the ESP layer of IPsec, which then encrypts and authenticates the IPsec data plane traffic. This design allowed us to avoid building out IKEv2 Initiator logic, and makes the Connector easier to maintain using our existing TLS libraries.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Thus, upgrading Cloudflare One Appliance to PQ encryption was just a matter of upgrading TLS 1.2 to TLS 1.3 with hybrid ML-KEM â something weâve done many times on different products at Cloudflare.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h3 id=\&quot;how-do-i-turn-this-on-and-what-does-it-cost\&quot;&gt;How do I turn this on? And what does it cost?&lt;/h3&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#how-do-i-turn-this-on-and-what-does-it-cost\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;As always, this upgrade to Cloudflare IPsec comes at no extra cost to our customers. Because we believe that a secure and private Internet should be accessible to all, weâre on a mission to include PQC in all our &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-cryptography-ga/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;products&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, without &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/you-dont-need-quantum-hardware/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;specialized hardware&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, at &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-crypto-should-be-free/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;no extra cost&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to our customers and end users.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Customers using the Cloudflare One Appliance obtained this upgrade to PQC in version 2026.2.0 (released 2026-02-11). The upgrade is pushed automatically (with no customer action required) according to each applianceâs configured interrupt window.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For customers using Cloudflare IPsec with another vendorâs branch connector appliance, we will be interoperating with these once more support for &lt;a href=\&quot;https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;draft-ietf-ipsecme-ikev2-mlkem&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; comes online. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/security-week/pq-ipsec-beta/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;You can also contact us&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; directly to get access to closed beta and request that we interoperate with a specific vendorâs branch connector.&lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;the-full-picture-post-quantum-sase\&quot;&gt;The full picture: post-quantum SASE&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-full-picture-post-quantum-sase\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;The value proposition for a post-quantum SASE is clear: organizations can obtain immediate end-to-end protection for their private network traffic by sending it over tunnels protected by hybrid ML-KEM. This protects traffic fromÂ  harvest-now-decrypt-later attacks, even if the individual applications in the corporate network are not yet upgraded to PQC.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/xK6FEbQYw9vLJKgx0bHp6/c4b584cc95adc5f8320d03c86b8fe38c/Cloudflare-s_post-quantum_SASE_2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;2402\&quot; height=\&quot;1266\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;The diagram above shows how post-quantum hybrid ML-KEM is offered in various Cloudflare One network configurations.Â  It includes the following on-ramps:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;clientless (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-zero-trust/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;TLS 1.3 with hybrid ML-KEM&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; (assuming the browser supports hybrid ML-KEM))&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare One Client (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-warp/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;MASQUE over TLS 1.3 with hybrid ML-KEM&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; initiated by the device client)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare IPsec on-ramp (as described in this blog)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;and the following off-ramps:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare Tunnel off-ramp (&lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-tunnel/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;TLS 1.3 with hybrid ML-KEM tunnel&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; initiated by the cloudflared server agent)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Cloudflare IPsec off-ramp (as described in this blog)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;The diagram below highlights a sample network configuration that uses the Cloudflare One Client on-ramp to connect a device to a server behind a Cloudflare One Appliance offramp. The end user&amp;#39;s device connects to the Cloudflare network (link 1) using &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-warp/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;MASQUE with hybrid ML-KEM&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. The traffic then travels across Cloudflareâs global network over TLS 1.3 with hybrid ML-KEM (link 2). Traffic then leaves the Cloudflare network over a post-quantum Cloudflare IPsec link (link 3) that is terminated at a Cloudflare One Appliance appliance. Finally it connects to a server inside the customerâs environment. Traffic is protected by post-quantum cryptography as it travels over the public Internet, even if the server itself does not support post-quantum cryptography.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2mrF4j8VDBGOzGEQNCobo4/b78ae6bef6f1152d92c9f63102aa8491/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;671\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Finally, we note that traffic that on-ramps to Cloudflare One and then egresses to the public Internet can also be protected by our post-quantum &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/traffic-policies/http-policies/tls-decryption/#post-quantum-support\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Gateway&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, our Secure Web Gateway (SWG).Â  Hereâs a diagram showing how the SWG works:&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3j3uN3x5oyUZBWbXIECxzA/9f2fd83cc567c8e511de08dd86ee462f/image2.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1488\&quot; height=\&quot;700\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;Â As discussed in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-zero-trust/#quantum-safe-swg-end-to-end-pqc-for-access-to-third-party-web-applications\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;an earlier blog post&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, our SWG can already support hybrid ML-KEM on traffic from SWG to the origin server (as long as the origin supports hybrid ML-KEM), and on traffic from the client to the SWG (if the client supports hybrid ML-KEM, which is the case for most modern browsers). Importantly, any traffic that onramps to the SWG via a device that has Cloudflare One Client installed is still protected with hybrid ML-KEM â even if the web browser itself does not yet support post-quantum cryptography. This is due to the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-warp/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;post-quantum MASQUE tunnel&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; that the Cloudflare One Client establishes to Cloudflareâs global network.Â  The same is true of traffic that onramps to the SWG via a post-quantum Cloudflare IPsec tunnel.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Putting it all together, Cloudflare One now offers post-quantum encryption on our TLS, MASQUE and IPsec on-ramp and off-ramps, and for private network traffic, and to traffic that egresses to the public Internet via our SWG.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n    &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n      &lt;h2 id=\&quot;the-future-is-quantum-safe\&quot;&gt;The future is quantum-safe&lt;/h2&gt;\n      &lt;a href=\&quot;#the-future-is-quantum-safe\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n      &lt;/a&gt;\n    &lt;/div&gt;\n    &lt;p&gt;By completing the post-quantum SASE equation with Cloudflare IPsec and the Cloudflare One Appliance, we have extended post-quantum encryption across all our major on-ramps and off-ramps. We have intentionally chosen the path of interoperability and simplicity â the hybrid ML-KEM approach that the IETF and NIST have championed, rather than locking our customers into proprietary implementations, âciphersuite bloat,&amp;quot; or unnecessary hardware upgrades.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is the promise of Cloudflare One: a SASE platform that is not only faster and more reliable than the legacy architectures it replaces, but one that provides post-quantum encryption. Whether you are securing a remote workerâs browser or a multi-gigabit data center link, you can now do so with the confidence that your data is protected from harvest-now-decrypt-later attacks and other future-looking threats.Â Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/pqc/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Sign up here&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get a full demo of our post-quantum capabilities across the Cloudflare One SASE platform, or &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/security-week/pq-ipsec-beta/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;register here&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to get on the list for the Cloudflare IPsec closed beta. alt="Mari Galicer" width="62" height="62"/></a><div class="author-name-tooltip"><a href="/author/mari/" class="fw4 f3 no-underline black mr3">Mari Galicer</a></div></li></ul><section class="post-full-content"><div class="mb2 gray5">9 min read</div><img class="mr2" src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3IqnOWiAzwo3glLQod9yck/cf6f2d1bff2c43462661ef9d70955e93/Hero_Image.png" alt=""/><div class="post-content lh-copy gray1"><p></p><p>Cloudflare Radar already offers a wide array of <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/security/"><u>security insights</u></a> â from application and network layer attacks, to malicious email messages, to digital certificates and Internet routing.</p><p>And today weâre introducing even more. We are launching several new security-related data sets and tools on Radar:Â </p><ul><li><p>We are extending our post-quantum (PQ) monitoring beyond the client side to now include origin-facing connections. We have also released a new tool to help you check any website&#39;s post-quantum encryption compatibility.Â </p></li><li><p>A new Key Transparency section on Radar provides a public dashboard showing the real-time verification status of Key Transparency Logs for end-to-end encrypted messaging services like WhatsApp, showing when each log was last signed and verified by Cloudflare&#39;s Auditor. The page serves as a transparent interface where anyone can monitor the integrity of public key distribution and access the API to independently validate our Auditorâs proofs.Â </p></li><li><p>Routing Security insights continue to expand with the addition of global, country, and network-level information about the deployment of ASPA, an emerging standard that can help detect and prevent BGP route leaks.Â </p></li></ul>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="measuring-origin-post-quantum-support">Measuring origin post-quantum support</h2>
      <a href="#measuring-origin-post-quantum-support" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2gs0x3zMZTxios168jT9xW/179d8959b5e0939835cf6facef797457/1.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="419" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>Since <a href="https://x.com/CloudflareRadar/status/1788277817362329983"><u>April 2024</u></a>, we have tracked the aggregate growth of client support for post-quantum encryption on Cloudflare Radar, chronicling its global growth from <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage?dateStart=2024-01-01&dateEnd=2024-01-31#post-quantum-encryption-adoption"><u>under 3% at the start of 2024</u></a>, to <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage?dateStart=2026-02-01&dateEnd=2026-02-28#post-quantum-encryption-adoption"><u>over 60% in February 2026</u></a>. And in October 2025, <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/pq-2025/#what-you-can-do-today-to-stay-safe-against-quantum-attacks"><u>we added the ability</u></a> for users to <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/adoption-and-usage#browser-support"><u>check</u></a> whether their browser supports <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/ssl/post-quantum-cryptography/pqc-support/#x25519mlkem768"><code><u>X25519MLKEM768</u></code></a> â a hybrid key exchange algorithm combining classical <a href="https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc8410"><code><u>X25519</u></code></a> with <a href="https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/FIPS/NIST.FIPS.203.pdf"><u>ML-KEM</u></a>, a lattice-based post-quantum scheme standardized by NIST. This provides security against both classical and quantum attacks.Â </p><p>However, post-quantum encryption support on user-to-Cloudflare connections is only part of the story.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/67cvSmOaISIHjrKKRHKPzg/e0ccf032658904fd6beaa7de7340b561/2.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1380" height="266" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>For content not in our CDN cache, or for uncacheable content, Cloudflareâs edge servers establish a separate connection with a customerâs origin servers to retrieve it. To accelerate the transition to quantum-resistant security for these origin-facing fetches, we <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/post-quantum-to-origins/"><u>previously introduced an API</u></a> allowing customers to opt in to preferring post-quantum connections. Today, weâre making post-quantum compatibility of origin servers visible on Radar.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6KvV2meYLEPbNIQyHP6yji/9477a134c8f5f6a7aaecd6257cd59981/3.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1944" height="1046" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>The new origin post-quantum support graph on Radar illustrates the share of customer origins supporting <code>X25519MLKEM768</code>. This data is derived from <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/automatically-secure/"><u>our automated TLS scanner,</u></a> which probes TLS 1.3-compatible origins and aggregates the results daily. It is important to note that our scanner tests for support rather than the origin server&#39;s specific preference. While an origin may support a post-quantum key exchange algorithm, its local TLS key exchange preference can ultimately dictate the encryption outcome.</p><p>While the headline graph focuses on post-quantum readiness, the scanner also evaluates support for classical key exchange algorithms. Within the Radar <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/explorer?dataSet=post_quantum.origin&groupBy=key_agreement#result"><u>Data Explorer view</u></a>, you can also see the full distribution of these supported TLS key exchange methods.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5PBOoQSCcIAQrYezKp1pJU/d4218aba59deef6c21df53856a93040a/4.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1938" height="1030" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>As shown in the graphs above, approximately 10% of origins could benefit from a post-quantum-preferred key agreement today. This represents a significant jump from less than 1% at the start of 2025 â <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/explorer?dataSet=post_quantum.origin&groupBy=key_agreement&dt=2025-01-01_2025-12-31"><u>a 10x increase in just over a year</u></a>. We expect this number to grow steadily as the industry continues its migration. This upward trend likely accelerated in 2025 as many server-side TLS libraries, such as <a href="https://openssl-library.org/post/2025-04-08-openssl-35-final-release/"><u>OpenSSL 3.5.0+</u></a>,<a href="https://www.gnutls.org/"><u> GnuTLS 3.8.9+</u></a>, and <a href="https://go.dev/doc/go1.24#cryptotlspkgcryptotls"><u>Go 1.24+</u></a>, enabled hybrid post-quantum key exchange by default, allowing platforms and services to support post-quantum connections simply by upgrading their cryptographic library dependencies.</p><p>In addition to the Radar and Data Explorer graphs, the <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/post_quantum/subresources/origin/"><u>origin readiness data is available through the Radar API</u></a> as well.</p><p>As an additional part of our efforts to help the Internet transition to post-quantum cryptography, we are also launching <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/post-quantum#website-support"><u>a tool to test whether a specific hostname supports post-quantum encryption</u></a>. These tests can be run against any publicly accessible website, as long as they allow connections from Cloudflareâs <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/ips/"><u>egress IP address ranges</u></a>.Â </p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5dgwK3i7IeLLSUt5xnk4lf/276e25dda3389f6e0ad83a26acd08fec/5.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1341" height="278" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><sub><i>A screenshot of the tool in Radar to test whether a hostname supports post-quantum encryption.</i></sub></p><p>The tool presents a simple form where users can enter a hostname (such as <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/post-quantum?host=cloudflare.com%3A443"><code><u>cloudflare.com</u></code></a> or <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/post-quantum?host=www.wikipedia.org%3A443"><code><u>www.wikipedia.org</u></code></a>) and optionally specify a custom port (the default is <a href="https://www.iana.org/assignments/service-names-port-numbers/service-names-port-numbers.xhtml?search=443"><u>443, the standard HTTPS port</u></a>). After clicking &quot;Test&quot;, the result displays a tag indicating PQ support status alongside the negotiated TLS key exchange algorithm. If the server prefers PQ secure connections, a green &quot;PQ&quot; tag appears with a message confirming the connection is &quot;post-quantum secure.&quot; Otherwise, a red tag indicates the connection is &quot;not post-quantum secure&quot;, showing the classical algorithm that was negotiated.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3rfEG4dMlwR4FJkaKXTRWF/8cab135242057ce57f3b0e4a92be4cec/6.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="284" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/PXu3kjzwhVkb29kIFREOn/41785c06297e0667ff9e2b261ae9b819/7.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1341" height="189" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>Under the hood, this tool uses <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/containers/"><u>Cloudflare Containers</u></a> â a new capability that allows running container workloads alongside Workers. Since the Workers runtime is not exposed to details of the underlying TLS handshake, Workers cannot initiate TLS scans. Therefore, we created a Go container that leverages the <a href="https://pkg.go.dev/crypto/tls"><code><u>crypto/tls</u></code></a> package&#39;s support for post-quantum compatibility checks. The container runs on-demand and performs the actual handshake to determine the negotiated TLS key exchange algorithm, returning results through the <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/post_quantum/subresources/tls/methods/support/"><u>Radar API</u></a>.</p><p>With the addition of these origin-facing insights, complementing the existing client-facing insights, we have moved all the post-quantum content to <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/post-quantum"><u>its own section on Radar</u></a>.Â </p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="securing-e2ee-messaging-systems-with-key-transparency">Securing E2EE messaging systems with Key Transparency</h2>
      <a href="#securing-e2ee-messaging-systems-with-key-transparency" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/71b8HJK1iT0udJscvkqqI4/778efb329047fca017ff2cf4153330ad/8.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="419" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p><a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/privacy/what-is-end-to-end-encryption/"><u>End-to-end encrypted (E2EE)</u></a> messaging apps like WhatsApp and Signal have become essential tools for private communication, relied upon by billions of people worldwide. These apps use <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/ssl/how-does-public-key-encryption-work/"><u>public-key cryptography</u></a> to ensure that only the sender and recipient can read the contents of their messages â not even the messaging service itself. However, there&#39;s an often-overlooked vulnerability in this model: users must trust that the messaging app is distributing the correct public keys for each contact.</p><p>If an attacker were able to substitute an incorrect public key in the messaging app&#39;s database, they could intercept messages intended for someone else â all without the sender knowing.</p><p>Key Transparency addresses this challenge by creating an auditable, append-only log of public keys â similar in concept to <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/certificate-transparency"><u>Certificate Transparency</u></a> for TLS certificates. Messaging apps publish their users&#39; public keys to a transparency log, and independent third parties can verify and vouch that the log has been constructed correctly and consistently over time. In September 2024, Cloudflare <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/key-transparency/"><u>announced</u></a> such a Key Transparency auditor for WhatsApp, providing an independent verification layer that helps ensure the integrity of public key distribution for the messaging app&#39;s billions of users.</p><p>Today, we&#39;re publishing Key Transparency audit data in a new <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/key-transparency"><u>Key Transparency section</u></a> on Cloudflare Radar. This section showcases the Key Transparency logs that Cloudflare audits, giving researchers, security professionals, and curious users a window into the health and activity of these critical systems.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1LZ1DUzv0SCgBa0XqDURKP/26ccd8b0741073895cbb52aa7f1d5643/image11.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="1099" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>The new page launches with two monitored logs: WhatsApp and Facebook Messenger Transport. Each monitored log is displayed as a card containing the following information:</p><ul><li><p><b>Status:</b> Indicates whether the log is online, in initialization, or disabled. An &quot;online&quot; status means the log is actively publishing key updates into epochs that Cloudflare audits. (An epoch represents a set of updates applied to the key directory at a specific time.)</p></li><li><p><b>Last signed epoch:</b> The most recent epoch that has been published by the messaging service&#39;s log and acknowledged by Cloudflare. By clicking on the eye icon, users can view the full epoch data in JSON format, including the epoch number, timestamp, cryptographic digest, and signature.</p></li><li><p><b>Last verified epoch:</b> The most recent epoch that Cloudflare has verified. Verification involves checking that the transition of the transparency log data structure from the previous epoch to the current one represents a valid tree transformation â ensuring the log has been constructed correctly. The verification timestamp indicates when Cloudflare completed its audit.</p></li><li><p><b>Root:</b> The current root hash of the <a href="https://github.com/facebook/akd"><u>Auditable Key Directory (AKD)</u></a> tree. This hash cryptographically represents the entire state of the key directory at the current epoch. Like the epoch fields, users can click to view the complete JSON response from the auditor.</p></li></ul><p>The data shown on the page is also available via the Key Transparency Auditor API, with endpoints for <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/key-transparency/api/auditor-information/"><u>auditor information</u></a> and <a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/key-transparency/api/namespaces/"><u>namespaces</u></a>.</p><p>If you would like to perform audit proof verification yourself, you can follow the instructions in our <a href="https://blog.cloudflare.com/key-transparency/"><u>Auditing Key Transparency blog post</u></a>. We hope that these use cases are the first of many that we publish in this Key Transparency section in Radar â if your company or organization is interested in auditing for your public key or related infrastructure, you can <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/lp/privacy-edge/"><u>reach out to us here</u></a>.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="tracking-rpki-aspa-adoption">Tracking RPKI ASPA adoption</h2>
      <a href="#tracking-rpki-aspa-adoption" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2LAbrwY9ziVbe1BzfUyl7K/821a40f86c62dd9b44f7bcaee018dd28/10.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1999" height="419" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>While the <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/glossary/what-is-bgp/"><u>Border Gateway Protocol (BGP)</u></a> is the backbone of Internet routing, it was designed without built-in mechanisms to verify the validity of the paths it propagates. This inherent trust has long left the global network vulnerable to route leaks and hijacks, where traffic is accidentally or maliciously detoured through unauthorized networks.</p><p>Although <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Public_Key_Infrastructure"><u>RPKI</u></a> and <a href="https://www.arin.net/resources/manage/rpki/roas/"><u>Route Origin Authorizations (ROAs)</u></a> have successfully hardened the origin of routes, they cannot verify the path traffic takes between networks. This is where <a href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-sidrops-aspa-verification/"><u>ASPA (Autonomous System Provider Authorization)</u></a><b> </b>comes in. ASPA extends RPKI protection by allowing an <a href="https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/network-layer/what-is-an-autonomous-system/"><u>Autonomous System (AS)</u></a> to cryptographically sign a record listing the networks authorized to propagate its routes upstream. By validating these Customer-to-Provider relationships, ASPA allows systems to detect invalid path announcements with confidence and react accordingly.</p><p>While the specific IETF standard remains <a href="https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/draft-ietf-sidrops-aspa-verification/"><u>in draft</u></a>, the operational community is moving fast. Support for creating ASPA objects has already landed in the portals of Regional Internet Registries (RIRs) like <a href="https://www.arin.net/announcements/20260120/"><u>ARIN</u></a> and <a href="https://labs.ripe.net/author/tim_bruijnzeels/aspa-in-the-rpki-dashboard-a-new-layer-of-routing-security/"><u>RIPE NCC</u></a>, and validation logic is available in major software routing stacks like <a href="https://www.undeadly.org/cgi?action=article;sid=20231002135058"><u>OpenBGPD</u></a> and <a href="https://bird.network.cz/?get_doc&v=20&f=bird-5.html"><u>BIRD</u></a>.</p><p>To provide better visibility into the adoption of this emerging standard, we have added comprehensive RPKI ASPA support to the <a href="https://radar.cloudflare.com/routing"><u>Routing section</u></a> of Cloudflare Radar. Tracking these records globally allows us to understand how quickly the industry is moving toward better path validation.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6SI6A5vd2bAp3QnBAsJFmZ/24e11445eb0309252d759e88dbf2ba62/11.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1600" height="876" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>Our new ASPA deployment view allows users to examine the growth of ASPA adoption over time, with the ability to visualize trends across the five <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_Internet_registry"><u>Regional Internet Registries</u></a> (RIRs) based on AS registration. You can view the entire history of ASPA entries, dating back to October 1, 2023, or zoom into specific date ranges to correlate spikes in adoption with industry events, such as the introduction of ASPA features on ARIN and RIPE NCC online dashboards.</p><p>Beyond aggregate trends, we have also introduced a granular, searchable explorer for real-time ASPA content. This table view allows you to inspect the current state of ASPA records, searchable by AS number, AS name, or by filtering for only providers or customer ASNs. This allows network operators to verify that their records are published correctly and to view other networksâ configurations.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/K97G5TC7O1MYwkvFbrdTl/85b27f807401f85d2bbe140f1611a034/12.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1278" height="466" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>We have also integrated ASPA data directly into the country/region routing pages. Users can now track how different locations are progressing in securing their infrastructure, based on the associated ASPA records from the customer ASNs registered locally.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/6mhZyfrHexdo1GDAoKZEd7/44b63675595a01939fa4748210d8c482/13.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1848" height="1456" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>On individual AS pages, we have updated the Connectivity section. Now, when viewing the connections of a network, you may see a visual indicator for &quot;ASPA Verified Provider.&quot; This annotation confirms that an ASPA record exists authorizing that specific upstream connection, providing an immediate signal of routing hygiene and trust.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/3lVJY4fZWv3KaFdKwLHfAV/aeb2bc27bdccb6a9025345dbaed5b762/14.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="660" height="423" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>For ASes that have deployed ASPA, we now display a complete list of authorized provider ASNs along with their details. Beyond the current state, Radar also provides a detailed timeline of ASPA activity involving the AS. This history distinguishes between changes initiated by the AS itself (&quot;As customer&quot;) and records created by others designating it as a provider (&quot;As provider&quot;), allowing users to immediately identify when specific routing authorizations were established or modified.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/ZIlAn2l0sDTLCyEMMcBI9/871b8d7abffe17b3aee060502eaa4c1c/15.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="857" height="1021" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p>Visibility is an essential first step toward broader adoption of emerging routing security protocols like ASPA. By surfacing this data, we aim to help operators deploy protections and assist researchers in tracking the Internet&#39;s progress toward a more secure routing path. For those who need to integrate this data into their own workflows or perform deeper analysis, we are also exposing these metrics programmatically. Users can now access ASPA content snapshots, historical timeseries, and detailed changes data using the newly introduced endpoints in the<a href="https://developers.cloudflare.com/api/resources/radar/subresources/bgp/subresources/rpki/subresources/aspa/"> <u>Cloudflare Radar API</u></a>.</p>
    <div class="flex anchor relative">
      <h2 id="as-security-evolves-so-does-our-data">As security evolves, so does our data</h2>
      <a href="#as-security-evolves-so-does-our-data" aria-hidden="true" class="relative sm:absolute sm:-start-5">
        <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path fill="currentcolor" d="m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z"></path></svg>
      </a>
    </div>
    <p>Internet security continues to evolve, with new approaches, protocols, and standards being developed to ensure that information, applications, and networks remain secure. The security data and insights available on Cloudflare Radar will continue to evolve as well. The new sections highlighted above serve to expand existing routing security, transparency, and post-quantum insights already available on Cloudflare Radar.Â </p><p>If you share any of these new charts and graphs on social media, be sure to tag us: <a href="https://x.com/CloudflareRadar"><u>@CloudflareRadar</u></a> (X), <a href="https://noc.social/@cloudflareradar"><u>noc.social/@cloudflareradar</u></a> (Mastodon), and <a href="https://bsky.app/profile/radar.cloudflare.com"><u>radar.cloudflare.com</u></a> (Bluesky). If you have questions or comments, or suggestions for data that youâd like to see us add to Radar, you can reach out to us on social media, or contact us via <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#f88a999c998ab89b94978d9c9e94998a9dd69b9795"><u>email</u></a>.</p>
          <figure class="kg-card kg-image-card">
          <Image src="https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/5jAzDXss7PvszWkwGC0q2g/df14de40bf268052fac11239952fc1ed/16.png" alt="" class="kg-image" width="1200" height="267" loading="lazy"/>
          </figure><p></p></div></section><section class="post-full-content flex flex-row flex-wrap mw7 center mb4"><div class="post-content lh-copy w-100 gray1 bt b--gray8 pt4">Cloudflare's connectivity cloud protects <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/network-services/' rel='noreferrer'>entire corporate networks</a>, helps customers build <a target='_blank' href='https://workers.cloudflare.com/' rel='noreferrer'>Internet-scale applications efficiently</a>, accelerates any <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/performance/accelerate-internet-applications/' rel='noreferrer'>website or Internet application</a>, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/ddos/' rel='noreferrer'>wards off DDoS attacks</a>, keeps <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/application-security/' rel='noreferrer'>hackers at bay</a>, and can help you on <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/products/zero-trust/' rel='noreferrer'>your journey to Zero Trust</a>.<br/><br/>Visit <a target='_blank' href='https://one.one.one.one/' rel='noreferrer'>1.1.1.1</a> from any device to get started with our free app that makes your Internet faster and safer.<br/><br/>To learn more about our mission to help build a better Internet, <a target='_blank' href='https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/what-is-cloudflare/' rel='noreferrer'>start here</a>.
